We’ve come a long way this year, taking the <a href="http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/all-in-one-event-calendar/">All-in-One Event Calendar</a> through some major feature and performance upgrades and growing our plugin downloads to nearly 270k with no sign of stopping.  But don’t worry, we won’t let this award go to our heads, what we’ve achieved so far is just the beginning and we intend to make good on being “the most promising startup of 2012″ (and beyond).  Thanks to all who have believed in us and championed our product this first year and we can’t wait to show you what’s in-store next. Wordcamps (for the uninitiated) are meet-ups held all over the world bringing WordPress-ers of all skill levels and interests together … <a href="http://time.ly/featured-event-wordcamp-vancouver-2012/">Continued</a>";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:32:"http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/";a:1:{s:7:"creator";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:4:"Evan";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:40:"http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/";a:1:{s:7:"encoded";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:2728:"<p><a href="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/wordpress_icons1.jpg"><img class=" wp-image-18559 alignleft" title="wordpress_icons1" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/wordpress_icons1.jpg" alt="" width="270" height="247" /></a>Last week we had the pleasure of attending our first<a href="http://2012.vancouver.wordcamp.org/"> Wordcamp here in Vancouver</a> and it was an awesome experience. <a href="http://central.wordcamp.org/">Wordcamps</a> (for the uninitiated) are meet-ups held all over the world bringing WordPress-ers of all skill levels and interests together for day long or multi-day events to talk about everything from code, to design, to business management, to freelance etiquette and of course the future of the wonderful WordPress publishing platform.</p>\n<p>The importance of the these events to the WordPress community cannot be overstated, in fact the rise and popularity of WordPress to become, arguably <a href="http://www.forbes.com/sites/jjcolao/2012/09/05/the-internets-mother-tongue/">the web’s most dominant publishing platform</a> can be largely attributed to Wordcamps and <a href="http://wordpress.meetup.com/">WordPress meet-up</a> events happening around the globe that bring people together to share ideas, solve problems and advance their overall understanding of what is possible in the WP universe.</p>\n<p>It may seem strange to think of something that is essentially a big block of programming code garnering an international cult-like following but beautiful technology attracts a crowd (witness the<a href="http://theweek.com/article/index/229766/5-signs-that-apple-is-a-cult"> kingdom of Apple</a>).  With WordPress as an open-source, contributive platform this is especially the case.Wordpress is made and largely governed by it’s community of users and programmers, no single entity really controls it (although the company <a href="http://automattic.com/">Automattic</a> owns <a href="www.wordpress.com">wordpress.com</a> and manages the central code contributions to <a href="http://wordpress.org/">WordPress</a>). It is quiet possibly the web’s greatest example of a sophisticated, democratized communication platform, where the tools, the processes and the culture evolve in an open forum for all to see and participate in. It really is a beautiful thing.</p>\n<p>At Wordcamp Vancouver we caught up with one of the main organizers <a href="https://twitter.com/mor10">Morten Rand-Hendriksen</a> to talk about why Wordcamps make the WordPress world go around.</p>\n<div class="entry-content-asset"><iframe width="940" height="529" src="http://www.youtube.com/embed/KU1PWcdCMBc?fs=1&feature=oembed" frameborder="0" Well Spent";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:4:"link";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:31:"http://time.ly/time-well-spent/";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:8:"comments";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:40:"http://time.ly/time-well-spent/#comments";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:7:"pubDate";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:31:"Wed, 10 Oct 2012 23:12:21 +0000";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:8:"category";a:6:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:16:"Thoughts on Time";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}i:1;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:8:"Antiphon";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}i:2;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:11:"experiences";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}i:3;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:6:"family";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}i:4;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:9:"happiness";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}i:5;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:4:"time";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:4:"guid";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:23:"http://time.ly/?p=16223";s:7:"attribs";a:1:{s:0:"";a:1:{s:11:"isPermaLink";s:5:"false";}}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:11:"description";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:286:"\x91Time well spent\x92\x97such a familiar phrase. If someone said it to you, you\x92d know what they were getting at. But where does the expression come from and what does it really mean? The first person (that we know of) to … <a href="http://time.ly/time-well-spent/">Continued</a>";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:32:"http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/";a:1:{s:7:"creator";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:8:"Jonathan";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:40:"http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/";a:1:{s:7:"encoded";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:6442:"<p><a href="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/fans-at-a-concert.jpg"><img class="alignleft size-medium wp-image-16411" style="border: 1px solid black;" title="Fans at rock show" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/fans-at-a-concert-300x224.jpg" alt="" width="300" height="224" /></a>\x91Time well spent\x92\x97such a familiar phrase. If someone said it to you, you\x92d know what they were getting at. But where does the expression come from and what does it <em>really</em> mean?</p>\n<p>The first person (that we know of) to speak of <em>spending</em> time, in the way that one might spend a currency, was Antiphon (c. 480-411 BC), and as we\x92ll see in future posts we owe a lot of our thinking about time to Greek writers and philosophers of this period. We don\x92t know too much about Antiphon, (although  this Wikpedia entry gives us a good start: <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antiphon_(person">en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antiphon_(person</a>)</p>\n<p>Anyway, what interests us here is not so much who Antiphon was, as what he said. The expression that concerns us is this: <em>the most costly outlay is the outlay of time</em>. Now, we normally say that the sorts of things that we can <em>spend</em> are resources\x97things like energy, money or effort. So a literal reading of this expression might suggest that time <em>is</em> a resource. But if that\x92s right, then time is going to be very much unlike other resources.</p>\n<p>For one thing, once it\x92s gone, time <em>cannot</em> be replaced, unlike money or effort. Nor can we find a \x91substitute\x92 as we might try to for a natural resource, like oil or coal. Quite unlike all of our other resources, we can\x92t control the <em>rate</em> at which we use up time nor can we store it.</p>\n<p>In fact, things get stranger still! If I spend some money, or energy, then in return I get something back. If I spend my money, I get <a href="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/usr_150707215554_hour-glass.jpg"><img class="alignright wp-image-16414" style="border: 1px solid black;" title="usr_150707215554_hour-glass" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/usr_150707215554_hour-glass.jpg" alt="" width="184" height="227" /></a>goods; if I spend energy, I get some effect. But, if I \x91spend my time\x92 doing something, then I don\x92t <em>seem</em> to <em>get</em> anything. How can this be right if we\x92re going to claim that time\x92s so <em>valuable</em>? If I can spend time without getting anything, surely that makes time our <em>least</em> valuable resource!</p>\n<p>But of course, we <em>do</em> get something when we spend our time on something. We get experiences. Experiences can be valuable. In fact, experiences can be <em>incredibly </em>valuable\x97just think of the ones that matter most to you. So, time\x92s a resource that you can\x92t store, that you can\x92t replace and that you can\x92t control. And you\x92re spending it on experiences every waking second of every single day of your life.</p>\n<p><img class="size-medium wp-image-16413 alignleft" style="border: 1px solid black;" title="stock-footage-people-walking-jogging-fishing-at-a-park-by-the-beach-at-sunset-in-hawaii" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/stock-footage-people-walking-jogging-fishing-at-a-park-by-the-beach-at-sunset-in-hawaii-e1349910092994.jpg" alt="" width="249" height="224" /></p>\n<p>Now if time is such a valuable resource, then what <em>should</em> we do with it? Are there particular sorts of behavior that are <em>better</em> uses ofour time than others? Recent research suggests that there are. Some research suggests that long working hours are negatively correlated with emotional satisfaction in adults<a title="" href="#_ftn1">[1]</a> and other research shows that people are happier with <em>experiential</em> purchases than they are with material purchases.<a title="" href="#_ftn2">[2]</a> We also know that time spent engaged in socially connecting activities, such as spending time with family, comprise the happiest parts of the day.<a title="" href="#_ftn3">[3]</a> All of which suggests that we would do well to try to work fewer hours, concentrate our financial resources on experiential purchases and spend more time with our friends and family. Maybe that\x92s just common sense.</p>\n<p>But if you want to feel like you\x92ve more time on your hands\x97that you\x92re more <em>time affluent</em>\x97one recent study suggests that the best thing that you can do is give it away for free.<a title="" href="#_ftn4">[4]</a> The study, led by <a href="https://marketing.wharton.upenn.edu/profile/388/">Cassie Mogilner at the University of Pennsylvania</a>, found that people who gave up their time to do things for others, found themselves with a feeling of having more time than those who were given <em>free</em> time.  Just as we have the saying, \x91you have to spend money to make money\x92, this looks to be a case where we need to spend time to make time! Given the connections mentioned above between time affluence and happiness, it looks like it might be a sound investment.</p>\n<div>\n<hr align="left" size="1" width="33%" />\n<div>\n<p><a title="" href="#_ftnref">[1]</a> Kasser, T. and Brown, K 2003. \x91<a href="http://www.kirkwarrenbrown.vcu.edu/wp-content/pubs/Kasser & Brown TBYT 2004.pdf">On Time, Happiness, and Ecological Footprints\x92</a>, in J. deGraaf (ed.), <em>Take Back your Time: Fighting Overwork and Time Poverty in America</em> (Berrett-Koehler, San Francisco, CA), 107\x96112</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><a title="" href="#_ftnref">[2]</a> Van Boven, L. and Gilovich, T. 2003, \x91<a href="http://dtserv2.compsy.uni-jena.de/ss2012/sozpsy_uj/31119589/content.nsf/Pages/97A6BE3B19E73ABFC1257A4600452E4A/$FILE/Boven on To Do or to Have.pdf">To Do or to Have? That Is the Question\x92</a><em>, Journal of Personality and Social Psychology</em>, 85, 1193\x961202</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><a title="" href="#_ftnref">[3]</a> Csikszentmihalyi, M and Hunter, J. 2003. \x91<a href="http://www.mendedreality.com/private/docs/CSIKSZENTMIHALYI2003.pdf">Happiness in Everyday Life: The uses of experience sampling</a>\x92, <em>Journal of Happiness Studies</em>, 4, 185-99</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><a title="" href="#_ftnref">[4]</a> Molinger, C., Chance, Z. and Norton, D. forthcoming. \x91<a href="https://marketing.wharton.upenn.edu/files/?whdmsaction=public:main.file&fileID=3722">Giving Time Gives You Time</a>\x92, <em>Psychological Science</em></p>\n</div>\n</div>\n";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:36:"http://wellformedweb.org/CommentAPI/";a:1:{s:10:"commentRss";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:36:"http://time.ly/time-well-spent/feed/";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:38:"http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/slash/";a:1:{s:8:"comments";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:1:"0";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}}}i:3;a:6:{s:4:"data";s:44:"\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\n\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";s:5:"child";a:5:{s:0:"";a:7:{s:5:"title";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:57:"Introducing What is <em>Time</em>? How do we measure it? Where does it come from? Is it outside of us or just in our heads? If a clock ticks in the forest and no one’s around, does it really tell the time? What is a <em>good time</em>? What is a <em>bad time</em>? Getting a little too deep for you? Well you may think that a calendar software developer has no business waxing philosophical about something as nebulous as time but you’d be wrong! We’re time geeks here to the extreme. We like to look at time from all sorts of different angles, and we love talking with people who do the same, that’s why were excited to introduce a our new guest blogger, Jonathan Tallant!</p>\n<p>Jonathan is a time philosopher at the <a href="http://www.nottingham.ac.uk/index.aspx">University of<em> </em>Nottingham</a>. That’s right. A <em><a href="http://www.nottingham.ac.uk/philosophy/people/jonathan.tallant">Time Philosopher</a>.</em> As far as we’re concerned that’s just<a href="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/a5oxpox2wlef9g3uspap.jpeg"><img class="alignright wp-image-15470" title="a5oxpox2wlef9g3uspap" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/a5oxpox2wlef9g3uspap-300x225.jpeg" alt="" width="240" height="180" /></a> one step down from <a href="http://images.epilogue.net/users/nathie/BadGuySorcererApril72.jpg">Time Sorcerer</a> and well above your common <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JwnjENpIyq0">Time Bandit</a>. Alas Jonathan is not involved in the direct manipulation of time per say but he does posit a variety of fascinating theories and themes on how humans perceive and experience time. As such we asked him to help us explore the concept of time experience as it relates to events, great and small. His first guest post appears next week and we’ll be hounding him for more whenever he’s got the (wait for it) – <strong><em>time! </em></strong></p>\n<p>Check out some of Jonathan’s videos on YouTube of the things we love here at Timely is coming across calendar users who really understand the potential of our All-in-One Event Calendar plugin to connect communities via cross-calendar sharing and make it easy for people to find the events they care about. That’s why starting this month we’re launching a new monthly blog series called <strong>Calendar Stories</strong> to highlight some of the best examples of our plugin being used around the world.</p>\n<p><a href="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/jacksonopolis1.jpeg"><img class="size-medium wp-image-14069 alignleft" title="jacksonopolis1" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/jacksonopolis1-300x300.jpeg" alt="" width="300" height="300" /></a>A few weeks ago the folks over at <a href="http://www.jacksonopolis.com/" target="_blank">Jacksonopolis.com</a> Tweeted us to show off their new community calendar set-up. Jacksonopolis is setting itself up to be the go-to source for community news and events for <a href="https://maps.google.ca/maps?q=Jackson+Michigan&ie=UTF-8&hq=&hnear=0x883d25593e337b6b:0xce45a6328e9bd551,Jackson,+MI,+USA&gl=ca&ei=pfhlUJPmH6TYigKh3ICwCg&ved=0CMYBELYD">Jackson, Michigan</a>. Co-founder and CEO of Jacksonopolis <a href="https://www.facebook.com/davidbuchanan">David Buchanan</a> was kind enough to answer some questions about how they’ve been using Timely’s All-in-One plugin to power their events calendar and why it’s important for communities like Jackson to have a unified events platform to stay informed and connected.</p>\n<h4>Could you describe what Jacksonopolis is and how it came to be?</h4>\n<p><em>Jacksonopolis showcases people, places, culture, and community in Jackson, Michigan. We came to life because of a dire need for our community to build pride, focus creativity and grow new economic sectors. Our city has been misrepresented for some time so our team is working hard to highlight the things which make our town so great. All content is submitted by the community and the site is supported by the generous local business and organizations that continue to make it great<strong><strong>.</strong></strong></em></p>\n<h4>What prompted the need for a more networked community events calendar?</h4>\n<p><em>We\x92ve run a new media company, Coefficient Media, since 2007 building websites and the community members came to us begging to build a well designed and usable central place for Jackson. For over 4 years we used our network to gather information and hold open meetings with the community to find their needs and wants. This is one of the reasons we love social networking; It\x92s tools like Facebook, Twitter and web portals, which enable communication and interactivity all around us. We set our focus to foster certain interactions, how to influence and share different events with friends, family, community members and leaders to have a more organized online experience.</em><strong><strong><br />\n</strong></strong></p>\n<h4>Why is a complete events listing important for your community?</h4>\n<div id="attachment_14071" class="wp-caption alignleft" style="width: 310px"><img class="size-medium wp-image-14071 " title="Jacksonopolis2" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/Jacksonopolis2-300x300.jpeg" alt="" width="300" height="300" /><p class="wp-caption-text">A local Jackson community event.</p></div>\n<p><em>While the idea of events listings and calendars are not new to a local community, we want to take it to the next level.  Technology is </em><em>changing the way we interact with our local community and we feel the need to connect more than ever. So much is happening all around us we need to calendar feature events, make them easy to share, intuitive to navigate, and able to subscribe to categories.</em></p>\n<p><em>Our goal is to tear down the existing roadblocks and let the community share and connect organically through the use of their everyday tools, like social media.<strong><strong> </strong></strong></em></p>\n<h3></h3>\n<h3></h3>\n<h3></h3>\n<h3></h3>\n<h3></h3>\n<h3></h3>\n<h3></h3>\n<h4>Why did you choose Timely’s All-in-One Events Calendar for the job?</h4>\n<ol>\n<li><em>Social integration.  We want the events to live in on Facebook along with being associated with our website.</em>\n<p><div id="attachment_14070" class="wp-caption alignright" style="width: 310px"><a href="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/jacksonopolis3.jpeg"><img class="size-medium wp-image-14070" title="jacksonopolis3" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/jacksonopolis3-300x223.jpeg" alt="" width="300" height="223" /></a><p class="wp-caption-text"><em>The Jacksonopolis team hard at work.</em></p></div></li>\n<li><em>Cross Calendar Sharing.  We build a lot of calendars and the ability to link data from one to another is amazing.  With Timely, the calendar we built for the Art\x92s Council and the calendar for the Young Professionals network will have the same unified data structure!</em></li>\n</ol>\n<p> </p>\n<p>So what’s next for Jacksonopolis? David says they’re planning on syncing filtered event data between various community calendars all using the Ai1EC to create an events network powered by individuals and businesses across their region (that’s exactly what we designed it for!). Congrats to David and his team for building a great looking site with an awesome organizational mandate. If you live, work (or travel) in the Jackson MI area, <a href="http://Jacksonopolis.com" class="autohyperlink" title="http://Jacksonopolis.com" target="_blank">Jacksonopolis.com</a> should be your first stop for news and events.</p>\n";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:36:"http://wellformedweb.org/CommentAPI/";a:1:{s:10:"commentRss";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:51:"http://time.ly/calendar-stories-jacksonopolis/feed/";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:38:"http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/slash/";a:1:{s:8:"comments";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:1:"0";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}}}i:5;a:6:{s:4:"data";s:53:"\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";s:5:"child";a:5:{s:0:"";a:7:{s:5:"title";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:40:"Featured Event: Seattle Startup Day 2012</h2>\n<p>Okay it’s no secret that were obsessed with finding and sharing great events and that we sometimes give extra-special treatment to startups and technology events being that 1) we’re geeks and 2) <em>we’re a startup</em> but we love getting to events of all kinds especially when we can learn something new and talk to some fresh faces no matter what the industry or location. When we can we take our crack production crew (Okay, me) down to document what we see and get the nitty gritty on the event details, who’s involved and why it’s an important.</p>\n<p>Last weekend we had the opportunity to travel down to Seattle to check out the north-west coast’s premier event for start-up culture and camaraderie hosted by our friends at <a href="http://www.geekwire.com/">GeekWire</a> <a href="https://twitter.com/johnhcook">John Cook</a> and <a href="https://twitter.com/toddbishop">Todd Bishop</a>.</p>\n<p>Here’s John explaining why #gwstartupday is all about and why it’s their “marquee” event of the year:</p>\n<div class="entry-content-asset"><iframe width="940" height="529" for Creating a Curated Calendar";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:4:"link";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:52:"http://time.ly/tips-for-creating-a-curated-calendar/";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:8:"comments";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:61:"http://time.ly/tips-for-creating-a-curated-calendar/#comments";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:7:"pubDate";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:31:"Tue, 28 Aug 2012 20:31:13 +0000";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:8:"category";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:17:"Calendar Insights";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:4:"guid";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:22:"http://time.ly/?p=8240";s:7:"attribs";a:1:{s:0:"";a:1:{s:11:"isPermaLink";s:5:"false";}}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:11:"description";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:332:"The online events calendar has become a mainstay for many businesses and organizations the world over but often these calendars are treated as exclusive listings where the only events featured are the ones directly hosted or connected to the event … <a href="http://time.ly/tips-for-creating-a-curated-calendar/">Continued</a>";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:32:"http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/";a:1:{s:7:"creator";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:4:"Evan";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:40:"http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/";a:1:{s:7:"encoded";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:6403:"<p><a href="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/Screen-Shot-2012-08-28-at-1.01.54-PM.png"><img class="alignleft size-medium wp-image-8673" title="Screen Shot 2012-08-28 at 1.01.54 PM" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/Screen-Shot-2012-08-28-at-1.01.54-PM-300x220.png" alt="" width="300" height="220" /></a>The online events calendar has become a mainstay for many businesses and organizations the world over but often these calendars are treated as exclusive listings where the only events featured are the ones directly hosted or connected to the event publisher. This might seem like an obvious default for many businesses and organizations but for those months when only a few events are planned it can mean a rather sparse looking calendar, and empty calendars have a way of implying low organizational activity, not the most desirable impression you want to leave with your website visitors.</p>\n<p>For that reason one of the  things we champion here at Timely is the idea of the<a href="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/Screen-Shot-2012-08-28-at-1.17.42-PM.png"><img class="alignright size-medium wp-image-8675" title="Screen Shot 2012-08-28 at 1.17.42 PM" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/Screen-Shot-2012-08-28-at-1.17.42-PM-300x221.png" alt="" width="300" height="221" /></a> “Curated Calendar.” Over the last few years the internet has taken on an interesting new dynamic. As the information available online has exploded, a new social layer has been necessary to sift through the content (news, blogs, photos, videos etc) and separate the wheat from the chaff so to speak. This has given rise to a practice known as <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Media_curation">content curation</a>, usually dedicated <a href="http://www.brainpickings.org/">individuals</a> and sometimes whole <a href="http://flavorpill.com/newyork">companies</a> motivated by a mandate to filter and serve only the best of the best information on a certain topic or interest. When you curate content and you do it well, it can become a powerful brand marketing strategy as it builds you a reputation as a trusted and desirable source for top quality information on a certain topic, and if you can save people time and effort searching through all the choice the web offers them you’ll quickly develop a loyal following.</p>\n<p>Curating event content is just as important. Let’s say you’re a fundraising organization for cancer research, and you have 10 big fundraising events each year, galas, marathons, auctions etc. Spreading those events out over a 12 month/365 day calendar may leave you with a fairly empty looking events schedule month to month but if you also seek out relatable events you could fill your calendar with a diverse range of interesting and valuable opportunities for your members. For example: talks from <a href="http://www.ted.com/talks/jay_bradner_open_source_cancer_research.html">cancer researchers</a>, local or international <a href="http://www.worldcancercongress.org/">medical conferences</a>, book launches, <a href="http://www.webmd.com/prostate-cancer/features/fifty-years-of-milestones-in-cancer-research">research milestones</a>, member get-togethers- a whole range of event experiences that may not be directly tied to the organization itself yet would still enrich the learning and development of your members. Your members will seek out your calendar not only because of your events but also because they’ll recognize it as the definitive calendar for all events related to cancer research.</p>\n<p><img class="alignleft size-medium wp-image-8671" title="Screen Shot 2012-08-28 at 12.21.20 PM" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/Screen-Shot-2012-08-28-at-12.21.20-PM-300x168.png" alt="" width="300" height="168" /></p>\n<p>Obviously one daunting task of populating a calendar with outside events is the extra work it would require for administrators, and that’s where a little “machine curation” can come in handy. With Timely’s All-in-One Event Calendar we’ve taken a lot of the leg work out of populating your calendar by making it really easy to syndicate and subscribe to calendar feeds from other calendars, even non-Ai1EC’s. This means that when you find a complimentary events calendar you love, you can easily <a href="http://help.time.ly/customer/portal/articles/504373-how-do-i-import-a-calendar-from-outlook-google-calendar-ical-">subscribe to the .ics feed</a> and add it to your Ai1EC’s Calendar Feeds, tagging it and categorizing it as you desire.</p>\n<p>The events from the calendars you subscribe to are then fed into your calendar on a daily basis, maintaining all their information and formatting. You have thus provided a curated feed of relatable events to your calendar visitors and organization members with a simple one time set-up that will fill your calendar with fresh event content as it’s posted by the event publisher.</p>\n<h3>Here are 6 tips for creating a great curated events calendar:</h3>\n<ol>\n<li><strong>Think outside the typical “Event” definition – </strong>events could come from anywhere, they could be international or local, they could be attendance events or simply notable anniversaries or occasions that relate to your industry. Don’t get trapped in the typical “local event” model.</li>\n<li><strong>Make connections with sister organizations,</strong> share your events with theirs and vice versa.</li>\n<li><strong>Check the calendars of notable speakers, authors or personalities – </strong>seek out the notable individuals who relate to your brand  and subscribe to their calendar feeds.</li>\n<li><strong>Aggregate event feeds from local news media and tourism event calendars </strong>- They may not all be on the .ics format but if they are you can easily grab individual events or entire calendars into your Ai1EC.</li>\n<li><strong>Allow community event submissions</strong> – The All-in-One can be set up to allow community members to post their own events (with moderator review) a great way of gathering event content from your very own community</li>\n<li><strong>Subscribe to member calendars</strong> – If other members in your organization host events and feature them on event calendars (Ai1EC or otherwise) you can have their events feed into your calendar.</li>\n</ol>\n";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:36:"http://wellformedweb.org/CommentAPI/";a:1:{s:10:"commentRss";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:57:"http://time.ly/tips-for-creating-a-curated-calendar/feed/";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:38:"http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/slash/";a:1:{s:8:"comments";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:1:"4";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}}}i:7;a:6:{s:4:"data";s:44:"\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\n\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";s:5:"child";a:5:{s:0:"";a:7:{s:5:"title";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:36:"Feature width="282" height="300" /></a>Perhaps you’ve already heard but Timely is a “<em>start-up” </em>one of those fascinating creatures of modern business that compulsively seeks to innovate, disrupt and ultimately solve some issue or demand in our society, (even ones we’re not yet aware of).  The issue we seek to solve is the one of <em>event search and discovery,</em> namely how to help people find all the events happening in their given area and help people/businesses/organizations publish and connect events more easily.  After all, how we perceive our time is very much tied to the quality of the experiences we have with it and being fully aware of all the experiences available to us gives us the opportunity for that magical outcome of <em>time well spent</em>, and if we’re lucky even <em>the</em> <em>time of our lives. </em></p>\n<p>Having the time of our lives is exactly what we plan on doing this week at <a href="http://growconf.com/">GROW </a><a href="http://growconf.com/">Conference</a> (<a href="https://twitter.com/#!/search/#growconf">#GROWconf</a>) in Vancouver, one of North America’s (nay the world’s!) premier events for start-up culture, industry and dialogue.</p>\n<div><a href="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/happening_1339783300.jpeg"><img class="size-full wp-image-5804 alignright" title="happening_1339783300" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/happening_1339783300.jpeg" alt="" width="250" height="200" /></a>This is the sort of place where deals are made, funding can be found, partnerships ignite and small companies make the inroads they need to become BIG companies. It’s a place of networking for sure but it’s also a place of growth, real entrepreneurial growth not just in funding opportunities but in terms of intellectual evolution for what it means to be a successful start-up in today’s world of dynamic technology and design.</div>\n<div></div>\n<div>So much happens at this one event that it can be a little overwhelming; conferences (of course), seminars, guest speakers, workshops, tours, launches, after-parties, kite boarding! It’s a wonderland of entrepreneurial activity and spirit and this week it’s our <strong>feature event</strong>, not because we happen to be there or that it happens to be centered around the very nature of our business but because it exemplifies what we consider <em>a life changing event. </em></div>\n<div></div>\n<div><a href="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/Screen-Shot-2012-08-21-at-1.23.15-PM.png"><img class="alignleft wp-image-5809" title="Screen Shot 2012-08-21 at 1.23.15 PM" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/Screen-Shot-2012-08-21-at-1.23.15-PM-e1345580608856-300x277.png" alt="" width="240" height="222" /></a></div>\n<div></div>\n<div></div>\n<div>When you put so many <a href="http://growconf.com/sessions/?id=6#talks">great thinkers</a> and status quo shakers into a few <a href="http://growconf.com/venue/">city blocks of downtown Vancouver</a>, something magical happens, actually lots of little magical things happen to many different people in many different places. An entrepreneur or perhaps a budding one, may enter as one thing and come out another. It’s transformative and we happen to think that a truly great event should lead you to indelible experiences that shape you or your ideas in some transformative way.</div>\n<div>\n<p>This year at GROW we hope to be transformed and we hope to transform. We’re looking to share <a href="http://time.ly/event-search-calendar/">our ideas</a> about how events should be published and discovered online and we’re hoping those very ideas evolve in the process of sharing them.</p>\n<p>This week at Grow you can find Timely CEO <a href="https://twitter.com/riklogtenberg">Rik Logtenberg</a> and Timely co-founder and VP Community <a href="https://twitter.com/BradleyRoulston">Bradley Roulston</a> strutting their stuff down the busy conference halls and happy-hour pow-wows. Now this is a major upgrade with a lot of new features that we’re really excited about, but before we send you off on an upgrading / downloading frenzy read this <strong>IMPORTANT NOTICE:</strong></p>\n<p>Due to a slight bug in the previous version of the Ai1EC (v1.7.1) current 1.7.1 users will need to download a special patch plugin in order to have a trouble free-upgrade (If you’re installing from scratch or from an earlier version like 1.7 then you can simply download the v1.8 Premium directly from <a href="http://time.ly">Time.ly)</a>.</p>\n<p>For all you 1.7.1 users watch this <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ex2d3oqMTSU&feature=youtu.be">quick tutorial video</a> on how to do the upgrade</p>\n<p><img class="alignright wp-image-110" style="border: 1px solid black;" title="Screen Shot 2012-07-26 at 4.06.58 PM" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/Screen-Shot-2012-07-26-at-4.06.58-PM-e1343428763313-1024x741.png" alt="" width="400" height="289" /></p>\n<p>Now on to the fun stuff! Version 1.8 Premium includes a feature that gives you an entirely new way of displaying your calendar to your website visitors. It’s called <strong>Posterboard View</strong> and it may very well alter the <em><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calendar">entire </a></em><em><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calendar">course of event calendar evolution</a>. </em>Okay a little heavy on the hyperbole but for us Posterboard represents something truly different for the online events calendar. You see Posterboard view breaks with the grid / list layout of the traditional calendar by presenting your events more like a community bulletin board, with emphasis on the featured image of each event. It’s more visual, more attractive and ultimately more engaging for your calendar visitors. Posterboard will work especially well for users like clubs, concert halls, <a href="http://spiritbar.inthekoots.com/">music venues</a>, and theatres who regularly post photos or artwork for their events (i.e. concert posters) and want to show them off without having to click to get the event details.  It’s almost like <a href="http://pinterest.com/clevercaliber/calendars-of-our-lives/">Pinterest</a> for events ; )</p>\n<p><a href="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/Screen-Shot-2012-07-30-at-12.29.26-PM-e1343677109837.png"><img class="alignleft size-full wp-image-124" style="border: 1px solid black; margin-top: 2px; margin-bottom: 2px;" title="Screen Shot 2012-07-30 at 12.29.26 PM" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/Screen-Shot-2012-07-30-at-12.29.26-PM-e1343677109837.png" alt="" width="360" height="202" /></a>Also new in this release is the long awaited<a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Ryd5s06KezI&feature=plcp" target="_blank"> Facebook Integration</a> feature that allows Ai1EC owners to import and export events directly to and from Facebook. This feature allows you to subscribe to your personal events on Facebook (i.e. the ones you’ve joined orcreated) as well as the eventsof friends, fan/business pages and groups.</p>\n<p><strong>Other new features include:</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li>The ability to lock the calendar to a particular view (Posterboard, month, agenda, etc)</li>\n<li>Improved (refactored) javascript which should dramatically reduce conflicts with other plugins</li>\n<li>A variety of UI / UX improvements</li>\n<li>Our new “Timely” branding : )</li>\n</ul>\n<div>Well we hope you enjoy version 1.8 and we look forward to your feedback. As always for technical support or development inquiries contact us at <a href="help.time.ly">help.time.ly.</a></div>\n<p> </p>\n";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:36:"http://wellformedweb.org/CommentAPI/";a:1:{s:10:"commentRss";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:83:"http://time.ly/announcing-v1-8-with-posterboard-view-and-facebook-integration/feed/";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:38:"http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/slash/";a:1:{s:8:"comments";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:2:"19";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}}}i:9;a:6:{s:4:"data";s:56:"\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";s:5:"child";a:5:{s:0:"";a:7:{s:5:"title";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:45:"The Event";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:4:"link";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:37:"http://time.ly/event-search-calendar/";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:8:"comments";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:46:"http://time.ly/event-search-calendar/#comments";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:7:"pubDate";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:31:"Fri, 27 Jul 2012 16:55:16 +0000";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:8:"category";a:6:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:16:"Thoughts on Time";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}i:1;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:8:"calendar";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}i:2;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:8:"discover";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}i:3;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:7:"google+";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}i:4;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:5:"index";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}i:5;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:6:"search";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:4:"guid";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:20:"http://time.ly/?p=91";s:7:"attribs";a:1:{s:0:"";a:1:{s:11:"isPermaLink";s:5:"false";}}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:11:"description";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:318:"At Timely our goal is to help people find events online.  It’s really that simple. Only it’s not. And it’s not because the majority of online calendar / event systems are designed with exclusivity in mind.  Facebook wants you to … <a href="http://time.ly/event-search-calendar/">Continued</a>";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:32:"http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/";a:1:{s:7:"creator";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:4:"Evan";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:40:"http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/";a:1:{s:7:"encoded";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:4327:"<p><a href="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/Screen-Shot-2012-07-27-at-9.53.20-AM.png"><img class="wp-image-92 alignnone" style="margin-left: 3px; margin-right: 3px; border: 1px solid black;" title="Screen Shot 2012-07-27 at 9.53.20 AM" src="http://time.ly/wp-timely/assets/Screen-Shot-2012-07-27-at-9.53.20-AM-1024x576.png" alt="" width="564" height="317" /></a></p>\n<p>At Timely our goal is to help people find events online.  It’s really that simple. Only it’s not.</p>\n<p>And it’s not because the majority of online calendar / event systems are designed with exclusivity in mind.  <a href="https://www.facebook.com/help/events">Facebook</a> wants you to post all your events within it’s system, <a href="http://www.google.com/+/learnmore/events/">Google+</a>, <a href="http://eventful.com/vancouver/events">Eventful</a>, <a href="http://www.eventbrite.com/">Eventbrite</a>, <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/osview/canvas?_ch_page_id=1&_ch_panel_id=1&_ch_app_id=30&_applicationId=2000&_ownerId=43091468&osUrlHash=61Ks&trk=hb_side_apps">Linkedin</a>… the list goes on. These are all great systems, systems that we use routinely but the trouble is they’re big proprietary systems from big exclusive companies that also compete with each other and so the end result is a wildly fractured event index for any one place or time. If you were visiting Vancouver for example and you wanted to find out what’s going on. Where would you search? The locals might have their spots, and if you knew enough people in Vancouver maybe you could tap into some Facebook events,  but there would be no way to see a fully comprehensive list of all the events happening in the city unless you wanted to visit 10 different event calendar websites and even then you still might miss something.  The crux of the issue is that these systems don’t talk to each other, Facebook Event’s won’t play nice with Google+ events and probably never will. The same goes for an infinite number of proprietary community and regional calendar systems. They all want to be the best <em>event destination</em> and in doing so they’ve scattered the event information for the event seeker.</p>\n<p>So what we’re doing at Timely ultimately is to try and solve a very complex societal issue: how do we, as a plugged in, technologically advanced culture become “in the know?” How do we make events, <em>all events</em> searchable, discoverable and shareable online?</p>\n<p>It’s a big question, one that compels us every day. In order to solve it we’re developing tools like <a href="http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/all-in-one-event-calendar/">The All-in-One Event Calendar (Ai1EC)</a> a free plugin for <a href="http://wordpress.org/">WordPress</a> that allows website owners to share and connect their events into an event network so that creating an event once on your own website can send it out to anyone else who subscribes to your calendar. It’s cross-compatible with Google Calendar, iCal, MS Outlook (pretty much any system that uses <strong>.ics</strong> feeds) and most recently <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Ryd5s06KezI&feature=plcp">Facebook Events</a> and we plan on adding more compatibility with other event systems in future releases.  What’s more, when you use the Ai1EC you can choose to send the data of your events into <strong>The Timely Network,</strong> an event index we’re developing that will aide people in their search for events online, no matter what city, town or mountain hamlet they happen to be in.  The Timely Network is still in its infancy but with each new event you post to your Ai1EC calendar you add to a searchable database that will make those events more discoverable to search engines.</p>\n<p>At Timely we’re not trying to be the next big event destination, we’re trying to give <em><strong>You</strong></em> the Calendar user the tools you need to become that on your own.</p>\n<p>For more information on how we use event data please read our <a href="http://time.ly/all-in-one-event-calendar-privacy-policy/">privacy policy</a> or contact us at <a class="autohyperlink" href="mailto:info@time.ly" title="mailto:info@time.ly">info@time.ly</a></p>\n";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:36:"http://wellformedweb.org/CommentAPI/";a:1:{s:10:"commentRss";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:42:"http://time.ly/event-search-calendar/feed/";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:38:"http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/slash/";a:1:{s:8:"comments";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:1:"1";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}}}}}s:27:"http://www.w3.org/2005/Atom";a:1:{s:4:"link";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:0:"";s:7:"attribs";a:1:{s:0:"";a:3:{s:4:"href";s:20:"http://time.ly/feed/";s:3:"rel";s:4:"self";s:4:"type";s:19:"application/rss+xml";}}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}s:44:"http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/syndication/";a:2:{s:12:"updatePeriod";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:6:"hourly";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}s:15:"updateFrequency";a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:"data";s:1:"1";s:7:"attribs";a:0:{}s:8:"xml_base";s:0:"";s:17:"xml_base_explicit";b:0;s:8:"xml_lang";s:0:"";}}}}}}}}}}}}s:4:"type";i:128;s:7:"headers";a:16:{s:6:"server";s:12:"nginx/1.0.15";s:12:"content-type";s:23:"text/xml; Colors in the default design come in tan, yellow and silvery grey which lends a polished appearance to the theme. Tumblera comes with a selection of page additions: image presentation, famous quotes, video inserts and more. In the main layout there is space for a post, adding media, and below the content are areas with the writers’ photo and bio, social sharing and RSS subscription options and a related posts areas. One-click .htaccess WordPress security protection. Protects wp-config.php, \nbb-config.php, php.ini, php5.ini, install.php and readme.html with .htaccess security protection. One-click Website Maintenance Mode \n(HTTP 503). Additional website security checks: DB errors off, file and folder permissions check... System Info: PHP, MySQL, OS, \nServer, Memory Usage, IP, SAPI, DNS, Max Upload... Built-in .htaccess file editing, uploading and downloading.</p>\n\n<h4>Why is .htaccess Website Security So Much Better Than Any Other Type of Website Security?</h4>\n\n<p>The answer is very simple - .htaccess files are processed first before any other code on your website. In other words, \nhackers malicious scripts are stopped by BulletProof Security .htaccess files before those scripts even have a chance to \nreach the php coding in WordPress. BulletProof Security uses .htaccess website security files, which are specific to \nApache Linux Servers. Please read the FAQ page for Server compatibility questions.</p>\n\n<h4>BulletProof Security Fast and Simple with No Manual Configuration Required</h4>\n\n<p>The BulletProof Security WordPress Security plugin is designed to be a fast, simple and one click security plugin to \nadd .htaccess website security protection for your WordPress website. Activate .htaccess website security and .htaccess \nwebsite under maintenance modes from within your WordPress Dashboard - no FTP required. The BulletProof Security \nWordPress plugin is a one click security solution that creates, copies, renames, moves or writes to the provided \nBulletProof Security .htaccess master files. BulletProof Security protects both your Root website folder and wp-admin \nfolder with .htaccess website security protection, as well as providing additional website security protection.</p>\n\n<p>BulletProof Security allows you to add .htaccess website security protection from within the WordPress Dashboard so \nthat you do not have to access your website via FTP or your Web Host Control Panel in order to add website security \nprotection for your WordPress site. BulletProof Security Modes: Root .htaccess security protection, wp-admin .htaccess \nsecurity protection, Deny All .htaccess self protection, WordPress default .htaccess mode and .htaccess Maintenance \nMode (503 Website Under Maintenance). In BulletProof Security Mode your WordPress website is protected from XSS, RFI, \nCRLF, CSRF, Base64, Code Injection and SQL Injection hacking attempts.</p>\n\n<h4>BulletProof Security Maintenance Mode</h4>\n\n<p>BulletProof Security Maintenance Mode allows you to create your custom website under maintenance page within BulletProof Security \nand activate Maintenance Mode to put your website in maintenance mode. Maintenance Mode allows website developers or\nwebsite owners to access and work on a website while a 503 Website Under Maintenance page is displayed to\nall other visitors to the website. Allow access to your WordPress Dashboard for only yourself or add additional IP \naddresses to allow mulitple IP addresses access to your WP Dashboard while in maintenance mode.</p>\n\n<h4>BulletProof Security Additional Website Security Protection</h4>\n\n<p>WordPress is already very secure, but every website, no matter what type of platform it is built on should\nhave additional website security measures in place as a standard. The Master \n.htaccess files are pre-made and BPS writes .htaccess code that is customized for your website. There is nothing to figure out \nor to configure. Click the AutoMagic buttons (creates customized Master .htaccess files) and Activate BulletProof Modes (copies \nthe customized Master .htaccess files to your root and wp-admin folders). BPS has built-in Backup and Restore and \nan .htaccess File Editor for full manual editing control as well. BulletProof Website Security fast and simple. Enjoy!</p>\n\n<h4>Do I need to understand .htaccess code in order to use the BulletProof Security Plugin?</h4>\n\n<p>No, The .htaccess file creation is automated in BulletProof Security. Everything is automatically done for you.\nYou do not need to know or understand anything about .htaccess website security files in order to use the \nBulletProof Security plugin.</p>\n\n<h4>What do I do if I cannot log back into my website?</h4>\n\n<p>If you accidentally activated BulletProof Modes without first clicking the AutoMagic buttons or if you put your \nwebsite in Maintenance Mode and your IP address has been changed by your ISP and you cannot log back into \nyour website then you will need to use FTP or your Web Host Control Panel File Manager and delete the .htaccess file \nthat BPS created in your website root folder. BPS website security is done purely with .htaccess website security\nand nothing else is modified on your website. So simply deleting the .htaccess file in your website root folder\nremoves BPS website security and will allow you to log back in, use the AutoMagic buttons and activate \nBulletProof Mode again to protect your website again.</p>\n\n<h4>When I upgraded/updated BulletProof Security I saw an Alert. What does the Alert mean?</h4>\n\n<p>When upgrading/updating the BulletProof Security plugin you will see this WP Dashboard Alert. <strong>BPS Alert! Your site does not \nappear to be protected by BulletProof Security.</strong> As of BulletProof Security .47.2 WP Dashboard Alerts have been added to check \nyour Root and wp-admin .htaccess files to ensure that your website is protected. During the upgrade your .htaccess files will \nbe automatically updated and any new .htaccess security filters will be automatically added to your .htaccess files. In order \nfor BPS to automatically update your htaccess files you will need to stay current with BPS plugin updates and install the latest BPS \nplugin updates when they are available. Any custom htaccess code or modifications that you have made to your htaccess files will not \nbe altered, modified or changed. Activating BulletProof Modes again after upgrading BPS is no longer necessary.</p>\n\n<h4>Where can I find BulletProof Security troubleshooting steps & support?</h4>\n\n<p>Please see the <a href="http://www.ait-pro.com/aitpro-blog/297/bulletproof-security-plugin-support/bulletproof-security-wordpress-plugin-support/" title="BulletProof Security WordPress Support" rel="nofollow">BulletProof Security WordPress Support page.</a></p>\n\n<h4>Does BulletProof Security work on every type of Server?</h4>\n\n<p>BulletProof Security uses .htaccess website security files, which are specific to Apache Linux Servers. BPS is compatible with Apache Linux Servers\n and Nginx Servers - if the Nginx Server is on the frontend and an Apache Linux Server is on the backend). If you do not know what type of Server \n you have you can check your Server Type and Operating System on the BPS System Info page.</p>\n\n<h4>Does BulletProof Security Work on Windows IIS Servers?</h4>\n\n<p>Yes and No. .htaccess files are only used on Linux based hosting. You can install BulletProof Security if you have a Windows IIS\nhosted website to use the additional features in BPS, but you cannot Activate BulletProof Modes and use .htaccess files on Windows Hosting.\nPlease see this WordPress Codex <a href="http://codex.wordpress.org/Using_Permalinks#Permalinks_without_mod_rewrite" title="Permalinks without mod_rewrite">Permalinks without mod_rewrite</a> for more information.</p>\n\n<h4>Does BulletProof Security Work on Nginx Servers?</h4>\n\n<p>If you are using both Apache and Nginx together and Nginx is the frontend webserver and Apache is the backend Server\nused to process PHP then BulletProof Security will work on this type of combined Server Configuration. If you are only\nusing Nginx then an .htaccess file will not work. Nginx has its own rewrite module - HttpRewriteModule and the mod_rewrite equivalent\nof an .htaccess file has similar, but different coding and is added to an Nginx Server config file.\nNote: If you are not familiar with Nginx, then it should be noted that Nginx does not have a PHP module like apache?s mod_php, \ninstead you either need to build PHP with FPM (ie: php-fpm/fastcgi), or you need to pass the request to something that can handle PHP.</p>\n\n<h4>Are there any known issues or conflicts with other WordPress Plugins or Themes?</h4>\n\n<p>Occaisonally issues or conflicts do occur with other plugins, but they are always quickly resolved. BPS is compatible with all\nother Plugins and Themes. An .htaccess bypass / skip rule is all that is required to allow a plugin to do something that is blocked by BPS.\nPlease check the BulletProof Security <a href="http://www.ait-pro.com/aitpro-blog/2252/bulletproof-security-plugin-support/checking-plugin-compatibility-with-bps-plugin-testing-to-do-list/" title="BPS Plugin Testing and Fixes" rel="nofollow">Plugin Compatibility Testing and Fixes</a> page for the latest plugin bypass / skip rules.</p>\n\n<h4>What is the difference between BulletProof Security free and BulletProof Security Pro?</h4>\n\n<h4>BulletProof Security</h4>\n\n<ol>\n<li>.htaccess Website Security Protection</li>\n</ol>\n\n<h4>BulletProof Security Pro Feature Highlights</h4>\n\n<ol>\n<li>File Monitor - All WordPress and non-WordPress Files</li>\n<li>AutoRestore - Automatic File Restore</li>\n<li>Quarantine - Automatic File Quarantine</li>\n<li>.htaccess Website Security Protection</li>\n<li>Custom php.ini Website Security Protection</li>\n<li>F-Lock - Read Only File Locking</li>\n<li>Security Logging</li>\n<li>HTTP Error Logging</li>\n<li>PHP Error Logging</li>\n<li>Email Alerts</li>\n<li>Versatile Set of Pro-Tools</li>\n<li>Base64 Decoder / Encoder</li>\n<li><a href="http://www.ait-pro.com/aitpro-blog/3395/bulletproof-security-pro/bps-free-vs-bps-pro-feature-comparison/" title="BulletProof Security Features" rel="nofollow">View All BulletProof Security Pro Feature Details</a></li>\n</ol>\n\n<h4>Is BulletProof Security Network / MU / Multisite Compatible?</h4>\n\n<p>Yes. BulletProof Security contains AutoMagic buttons for Network / MU / Multisite websites. Both sub-directory and sub-domain Master .htaccess \ncode is written / created for your specific Network / MU site. BulletProof Modes should only be Activated on the Primary site. All sub sites \nare virtual and there is no need to Activate BulletProof Modes on sub sites. This will actually screw up your Primary site. BPS allows only \nSuper Admins to see the BPS menus in sub sites. BPS also works with Network / MU Domain Mapping.</p>\n\n<h4>Is BulletProof Security Compatible with subdomain websites and subdirectory websites?</h4>\n\n<p>Yes, BulletProof Security works on all types of WordPress installations including "Giving WordPress Its Own Directory" websites.</p>\n\n<h4>Is BulletProof Security automatically setup already?</h4>\n\n<p>Yes and No. You must be using a WordPress Custom Permalink structure for BPS to work correctly (every WordPress site should be anyway). If \nyou are not using a custom Permalink structure then you will get a warning message that Custom Permalinks need to be enabled when you access \nthe BulletProof Security Options page. BulletProof Security includes AutoMagic Master .htaccess file creation so that only one click is \nrequired to automatically create your Master .htaccess security files for your website, which you then Activate - BulletProof Mode. \nBulletProof Security also offers full manual control of editing the .htaccess files using the built-in File Editor. BulletProof Security is \ndesigned with everyone in mind: regular folks, Designers, Developers and Coders. BulletProof Security is designed to work with every type \nof WordPress installation: Single websites, subfolder websites, subdomain websites, "Giving WordPress its Own Directory" websites, \nNetwork / MU subdirectory websites and Network / MU subdomain websites. BulletProof Security will automatically create the correct Master \n.htaccess files for your website when you click the AutoMagic buttons. If you prefer to do everything manually then you would edit your \n.htaccess using the built-in .htaccess File Editor instead of using Automagic to automatically create your .htaccess files.</p>\n\n<h4>Can I add my own .htaccess code to the BulletProof Security .htaccess files?</h4>\n\n<p>Yes. Of course. The secure.htaccess and wpadmin-secure.htaccess Master .htaccess files already contain .htaccess security code that protects \nyour website against XSS, RFI, CRLF, CSRF, Base64, Code Injection and SQL Injection hacking attempts. Add any additional security filters or \nother .htaccess code to your Master .htaccess files or your currently active .htaccess files using the built-in .htaccess File Editor. The \nBulletProof Security Master .htaccess files contain help info and additional options within the .htaccess files themselves. htaccess files \ncan do a lot of neat things besides just providing website security protection. As of version .46.9 you can now also add any custom code \nto the Custom Code feature. Your custom .htaccess code will be saved to your WP DB permanently until you delete it. Please view the Read Me \nHelp button in Custom Code for specific details.</p>\n\n<h4>Does the BulletProof Security Plugin create or write the .htaccess files?</h4>\n\n<p>Yes, BulletProof Security creates customized .htaccess website security files with AutoMagic. BulletProof Security also offers full manual \ncontrol of editing both the BPS Master .htaccess files and your currently active .htaccess files using the built-in .htaccess File Editor. \nThe BPS Master .htaccess files have already been pre-made. When you click the AutoMagic buttons your .htaccess Master files are created with \nspecific code for your specific website with the correct RewriteRule and RewriteBase automatically added to your .htaccess files. You can \nadd additional code to the master .htaccess files, edit the .htaccess files or create completely new .htaccess master files from within the \nWordPress Dashboard using the built-in BPS File Editor - no FTP required - no Web Host Control Panel required. BPS could also just be used \nsimply as an online .htaccess file editor and manager. AutoMagic is great, but having both AutoMagic and full manual editing control makes \nBulletProof Security a very versatile website security protection tool.</p>\n\n<h4>Does BulletProof Security work with Git distributed version control system?</h4>\n\n<p>Yes, BulletProof Security works with Git, but does require some additional set up steps.
